  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f76dcabb-3e1b-4607-a6b5-676aa1a1f37e'
      });

Anna lightheartedly agrees to the game, but there’s something she hasn’t told Frankie–she’s already had her romance, and it was with Frankie’s older brother, Matt, just before his tragic death one year ago.<br /><br />TWENTY BOY SUMMER explores what it truly means to love someone, what it means to grieve, and ultimately, how to make the most of every beautiful moment life has to offer.</span>

<div id="review_1943936999" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1943936999" />
    <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader"><img alt="Aj the Ravenous Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557800982p2/30248594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1943936999?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aj the Ravenous Reader" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader">Aj the Ravenous Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=physically-owned-books">physically-owned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=emotionally-intense">emotionally-intense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1943936999" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4624364356777069362"><b> 3.5 stars! </b><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5231173.Twenty_Boy_Summer' title='Twenty Boy Summer by Sarah Ockler' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twenty Boy Summer</a> is certainly not what I expected and I don’t mean that in a negative way. In my opinion, this novel has a particularly originality to it that I couldn’t quite express eloquently but perhaps you’ll understand when you read the book. I picked this book up hoping to enjoy some warmth and fluff from a Summery read and although the story is in many parts heartwarming, there is nothing fluffy about it. In fact, it was mostly a sad read and I have to admit that I had to sn</span>
  <span id="freeText4624364356777069362" style="display:none"><b> 3.5 stars! </b><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5231173.Twenty_Boy_Summer" title="Twenty Boy Summer by Sarah Ockler" rel="nofollow noopener">Twenty Boy Summer</a> is certainly not what I expected and I don’t mean that in a negative way. In my opinion, this novel has a particularly originality to it that I couldn’t quite express eloquently but perhaps you’ll understand when you read the book. I picked this book up hoping to enjoy some warmth and fluff from a Summery read and although the story is in many parts heartwarming, there is nothing fluffy about it. In fact, it was mostly a sad read and I have to admit that I had to sniffle several times. <br /><br />Written in Ms. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=Sarah%20Ockler" title="Sarah Ockler" rel="nofollow noopener">Sarah Ockler</a>’s beautiful writing, this is a story about two best friends who try to move on after the death of one of the most important persons in both their lives by trying to hide and bury their grief in vacation and summer fun and attempting to meet twenty different boys for the duration of their summer. I don’t completely agree with their idea of fun and that’s probably my main complaint about the novel but to each her own, right?. In the end, the two girls achieve something they might not want but definitely need.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4624364356777069362" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Something beautiful. </i><br/><br/>Don’t let the light and fluffy title of this book deceive you. This book will make you cry, break your heart and then fill it up with hope again. <br/><br/>Twenty Boy Summer is an unforgettable story about friendships, love, loss, and finding the courage to let go.   <span id="freeText11159893966063867937" style="display:none"><i> Nothing ever really goes away - it just changes into something else. Something beautiful. </i><br /><br />Don’t let the light and fluffy title of this book deceive you. This book will make you cry, break your heart and then fill it up with hope again. <br /><br />Twenty Boy Summer is an unforgettable story about friendships, love, loss, and finding the courage to let go. This book was an emotional roller coaster ride, it made me smile one moment, cry the next, smile some more, cry again but at the end it left me feeling good. <br /><br />Sarah Ockler writing flows beautiful and has a lyrical feel to it. I always note my favourite quotes when reading a book and this one had so many that I loved, I had a hard time choosing just one to include in my review.<br /><br />I liked Anna she was a relatable character who I cared about and just wanted everything for her to turn out okay. But Frankie I struggle to like at times, she was too self centred, but I guess that is the way she dealt with her loss and by the end she mature somewhat. Matt and Sam were both sweet and amazing guys. <br /> <br />Overall I loved it and it will easily find a home on my favourites shelf.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1210019871826319174">One of the great things about Goodreads is that I get to capture books along the way, of which I normally would not.   <span id="freeText1210019871826319174" style="display:none">One of the great things about Goodreads is that I get to capture books along the way, of which I normally would not. This little cutie, a YA that I added on what I honestly think was almost on day one of GR, I actually came across just last week at my library. It was withdrawn, and only published in 2009... I thought this a shame, but gleefully snapped it up for 20c.<br /><br />This was a nice reminisce, I know there are no rules for who should read what, but I did feel funny looking back on those feelings I used to have - albeit through two young teens that I thought much, cooler and ‘together’ than I was at that age! Was I really that shy? Probably! Am I the intended audience for this? Probably not!<br /><br />This was a sweet coming of age, the mourning of the death of both brother and boyfriend for two best girlfriends, and the way they realise this unique relationship that each actually did hold to this boy. The loss of the boyfriend is not forever, as it was something that was not yet known, and such early days.<br /><br />These two girls were young and quirky, especially when together. The ‘clever’ one kept correcting the not so one on the mis-use of words. Like chartreuse/obtuse Heidelberg/Hindenburg exacerbate/exasperate provokial/parochial, you get the drift. <br /><br />The parents were a bit clueless, as were mine.. But I’m not going to be! I'm glad I read this, a genre that I just don't really read much of, maybe this has taught me something too!</span>

And I love that the book has all these references to sea glass, just like the awesomely beautiful cover. Genius! <br/><br/>And the pages between the fantastic cover are just as awesome.   <span id="freeText2054351781369380336" style="display:none">First off, let me just say that I LOVE the cover for this book! And I love that the book has all these references to sea glass, just like the awesomely beautiful cover. Genius! <br /><br />And the pages between the fantastic cover are just as awesome. This was undeniably one of my most favorite debut novels this year. Anna and Frankie were phenomenal characters. I totally understood Anna, I got her right away, but it took me the entire novel to finally get Frankie. Incredible. Ockler's depiction of Anna's emotions was beyond spectacular, I can't even begin to imagine how it felt to write that, because I know how it made me feel reading it. Wow. <br /><br />And how fantastic was the writing! I felt like I was summering in California and I have yet to visit! It was that good. Absolutely captivating. If you pick up one book this summer and are looking for more than chick lit fluff (not that chick lit fluff is bad, because personally I love it) I would recommend you pick this one up. </span>

<div id="review_83647223" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/83647223" />
    <a title="Arlene" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1746727-arlene"><img alt="Arlene" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1347048609p2/1746727.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/83647223?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arlene" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arlene" href="/user/show/1746727-arlene">Arlene</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Arlene by: </span>
      TBR Reduction Challenge #1 - Flannery 
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=read-2011">read-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=ya-contemporary">ya-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer83647223" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18312398994014157641"><i>Like the stars, fading with the halo of the vanishing moon. Like the ocean, falling and whispering against the shore. Nothing ever really goes away - it just changes into something else. Something beautiful.</i><br/><br/><br/>Don’t know why I put off reading <b>Twenty Boy Summer</b> for so long, but I’m very glad I was challenged to read this book sooner than later. I really.really.really enjoyed this story! It has all the ingredients of a well-written and perfectly plotted YA contemporary novel, and I fell for the chara</span>
  <span id="freeText18312398994014157641" style="display:none"><i>Like the stars, fading with the halo of the vanishing moon. Like the ocean, falling and whispering against the shore. Nothing ever really goes away - it just changes into something else. Something beautiful.</i><br /><br /><br />Don’t know why I put off reading <b>Twenty Boy Summer</b> for so long, but I’m very glad I was challenged to read this book sooner than later. I really.really.really enjoyed this story! It has all the ingredients of a well-written and perfectly plotted YA contemporary novel, and I fell for the characters immediately... from beginning to end.<br /><br />Now the plot seems a bit heavy at first glance because it involves a first love that dies too soon. Anna has had a crush on Matt, her best friend, since she was ten years old and on her fifteen birthday he reveals his true feelings for her and their light romance takes off. However, it’s a bit complicated because Matt’s sister is also Anna’s dear friend and Matt struggles with finding a way to share his true feelings for Anna to his sister Frankie, so they put it off and the unspeakable occurs. Matt’s life is stripped away too soon and the rest of the novel takes you on a journey of the meaning of friendship, grief and forgiveness.<br /><br />I came to care for all of the characters in this novel, especially and surprisingly the summer fling, Sam. I liked how the author left the ending slightly unfinished when it came to Sam because it allowed my imagination to float to my own conclusion for him and Anna possibly crossing paths in the future. <br /><br />Overall, I feel fans of books such as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6604794.The_Sky_Is_Everywhere" title="The Sky Is Everywhere by Jandy Nelson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Sky Is Everywhere</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7130546.Winter_Longing" title="Winter Longing by Tricia Mills" rel="nofollow noopener">Winter Longing</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/51737.The_Truth_about_Forever" title="The Truth about Forever by Sarah Dessen" rel="nofollow noopener">The Truth about Forever</a> will enjoy Ockler’s novel <b>Twenty Boy Summer</b>. Don’t miss out on this great novel that would make the perfect beach read. <br /><br />Thanks to Flannery for challenging me to read this book. You rock! XD<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18312398994014157641" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/333439619" />
    <a title="Ariie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8069625-ariie"><img alt="Ariie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1349321302p2/8069625.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/333439619?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ariie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ariie" href="/user/show/8069625-ariie">Ariie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Do yourself a favour and stay away from this book.</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Ariie by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/9643070-joanna">Joanna</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8069625-ariie?shelf=i-am-so-confused">i-am-so-confused</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8069625-ariie?shelf=no-self-respect">no-self-respect</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8069625-ariie?shelf=why-does-this-exist">why-does-this-exist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8069625-ariie?shelf=i-would-rather-do-math">i-would-rather-do-math</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8069625-ariie?shelf=flat-out-horrible">flat-out-horrible</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8069625-ariie?shelf=stupid-heroine">stupid-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8069625-ariie?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer333439619" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7321917133269323009">Let me start by saying that I thought this was going to be good. I really did.<br/><br/>But no. I absolutely hated this book. If you put Anna and Frankie's bullshit and Bella Swan's bullshit right beside each other, I might actually choose Bella's bullshit over this.<br/><br/>I reckon they are all on the same wavelength of stupidity. (Especially Bella and Frankie.) Take in the fact that this book has the same amount of hypocrisy and lack of self-respect as Twilight (and then some), but that Twilight has four books </span>
  <span id="freeText7321917133269323009" style="display:none">Let me start by saying that I thought this was going to be good. I really did.<br /><br />But no. I absolutely hated this book. If you put Anna and Frankie's bullshit and Bella Swan's bullshit right beside each other, I might actually choose Bella's bullshit over this.<br /><br />I reckon they are all on the same wavelength of stupidity. (Especially Bella and Frankie.) Take in the fact that this book has the same amount of hypocrisy and lack of self-respect as Twilight (and then some), but that Twilight has four books (technically), and this book is... single.<br /><br />If books were people, I'd see why this one was single. Forever alone in a void of nonexistent true friendship and self-respect along with unrealistic emotion. Pretty on the outside, something of a horror on the inside.<br /><br />I have no idea why anyone thought this was good. The fact that this book managed to reach three stars and is even close to four stars makes me want to shoot my foot.<br /><br />Now let me elaborate on the <i>thing</i> I liked about this book, and then the long list of what I absolutely <b>hated</b> about it.<br /><br /><b>What I liked:</b><br /><br /><b>1. Anna <i>with</i> Matt.</b><br /><br />The romance between Anna and Matt when the guy was alive was actually pretty sweet. (And more realistic than everything else in this book.) But however sweet it was, it really didn't convince me enough. There just wasn't enough backup. Sweetness doesn't make up for the fact that you have to back these things up.<br /><br /><b>What I hated:</b><br /><br /><b>1. Showing, not telling.</b><br /><br />I don't see why Ockler had to go on forever writing about how some scene looked like. I mean, I can do that too, but I also know how to balance these things out, and I'm fourteen. Telling, instead of showing, doesn't really make for good writing. It clumps everything up and takes up more time in the book. There was more on how the beach looked like than the development of... well, everything else.<br /><br /><b>2. You can't tell what kind of book this really is.</b><br /><br />On one side, you have two best friends wanting to have a fun summer. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Even if that was mostly because of Frankie pretending to be a slut. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />On the other, you have... Well, you have what was supposed to be sadness. The emotions weren't real enough to me. They felt superficial because of how the characters were portrayed as people. (If you could even use the word.) I just really didn't feel anything about it. This book was trying too hard to be two things at once. On one side, you've got the whole "Oh I'm a rebellious slut!" thing going on, and on the other, you have this... tragedy. (And I don't just mean the book itself.) It was all so fake.<br /><br />I mean, the reality of humans is that, if the situation was presented, most of us would resort to our more barbaric sides. But this book felt like that's exactly what they did (or at least in Frankie's case), and there was nothing about this book that had to resort to such actions (which will be presented in the last point).<br /><br /><b>3. Character and relationship development.</b><br /><br />I didn't feel anything for the characters except for annoyance, at best. Obviously this is a book where the relationships are pretty damn important, but obviously, it fails. Okay, so I could sort of see where Anna and Matt came from, but Anna and Frankie? How they could have ever come to be best friends, I just <i>do not</i> know. The way Frankie treated Anna was horrible. (Again, see the last point.) The relationships, at best, were unrealistic. At worst, they were destructive, emotionally abusive, distrustful, etc. To those of you who have read this book (or maybe not), I might seem like I'm exaggerating, but honestly? I'm not joking when I say Frankie spewed a lot of bullshit.<br /><br />Anna and Frankie are the main characters, but I see no development. Isn't there supposed to be, with Matt's death and whatnot? Why would there be a book just about how they wallow? I mean, if that was the case, surely it'd be more obvious in the summary? Nada. Anna stayed completely the same. Frankie stayed completely the same. Even at the end, when they had that whole friendship fallout and <i>apparently</i> made up, they were the same. The way they made up was just unbelievable. I've made up with friends quickly, sure, but come on. Maybe it could have been more believable if the characters themselves were.<br /><br />Sadly, they aren't.<br /><br />For the record, Sam had potential, but Ockler never did anything about that potential.<br /><br /><b>4. I'm just so confused.</b><br /><br />Ockler felt compelled to describe scenery as opposed to developing her characters, so everything went slow.<br /><br />Ockler also decided to randomly skip scenes that would give good feedback to the story, which also made everything slow.<br /><br />End of.<br /><br /><b>5. The virginity "issue". And Frankie's attitude.</b><br /><br />God. I absolutely, positively, 100% hated Frankie.<br /><br />Okay, I'm a very understanding person. So I get that she was hugely affected by her brother's death. I get that she had to get over it. I get that she had to rebel and all that. But seriously, I can't believe her nerve. Sure, I have a lot of nerve myself, but the difference between Frankie and I is that I have this thing called morals, this other thing called humanity, and this <i>other</i> thing called <i>a brain</i>.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I don't get it. Anna has sex with Sam, and then Frankie finds Anna's journal and gets mad at her. But then Frankie admits that she - wait for it, wait for it - never had sex with <i>anyone</i>. She, of course, had to <i>force</i> her best friend to lose her virginity though, because apparently, she (Anna) would be a loser otherwise.<br /><br />Right.<br /><br />If my best friends did that to me (trying to make plans for me to lose the V card) - and they never would - I would probably fuck them up. But the thing is, I'd never be forced into losing my virginity because of peer pressure. <i>No thank you.</i><br /><br />I guess I'm mostly pretty pissed about this because I'm (for the most part) a traditionalist romantic, so losing the V card isn't just a "whatever" thing to me. But Christ, what <i>real</i> friend would do that? I don't know if this was to be hip or something, but I'm not pleased with this. That is completely fucked-up, and for the record, the farthest description of best friendship I can think of.<br /><br />Honestly, what is this telling us? Frankie can mope and all that, and she can get mad at Anna for keeping Matt a secret from her (which is understandable seeing as how Anna wanted to forever keep it from her), but when her best friend loses her virginity because of her selfishness, all of a sudden everything's just great and fine and dandy.<br /><br />I'll say it again. What kind of best friend <i>does</i> that?!<br /><br />And again, maybe Ockler was trying to come off as "hip", or some crap, since all people <i>seem</i> to want to do these days is have sex and get high, but honestly?<br /><br />Are you freaking kidding me right now? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />ASDFGHJKL.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And then Sam's relationship with Anna was so awkward. On one hand he was sweet and everything, but on the other, he was also incredibly detached. Again, maybe this is my traditional, hopeless romantic speaking, but really - why are people so <i>stupid?</i><br /><br />Honestly, WTF. I get that she's leaving, but <i><b>WTF</b></i>. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I bet Ockler would have much better luck if she kept Matt alive and just did chick lit. (Because if this is chick lit, it really shouldn't be legal, and for the writing, not the themes.)<br /><br />But maybe she'd screw that up too. -_____-"</span>
  <a data-text-id="7321917133269323009" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50620706-alaina?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50620706-alaina?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1514535355" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18317669030812902282"><b>Pretty much the most adorable book I've read in October, so far. The month is young though..</b><br/><br/><i>Twenty Boy Summer</i> first made me think that someone was going to be a little adventurous in the boy department. Straight up thought she was going to commit and date 20 guys in one summer. 20 guys within a 3 month span.. could probably be doable.. but my eyes were like bugging out of my head. Thankfully, this book was nothing like that.<br/><br/>In this book, you will meet Anna and Frankie. Honestly, Anna was way mor</span>
  <span id="freeText18317669030812902282" style="display:none"><b>Pretty much the most adorable book I've read in October, so far. The month is young though..</b><br /><br /><i>Twenty Boy Summer</i> first made me think that someone was going to be a little adventurous in the boy department. Straight up thought she was going to commit and date 20 guys in one summer. 20 guys within a 3 month span.. could probably be doable.. but my eyes were like bugging out of my head. Thankfully, this book was nothing like that.<br /><br />In this book, you will meet Anna and Frankie. Honestly, Anna was way more likable than the other. Frankie just annoyed me to no end because of all of the unnecessary drama. However, their friendship was cute and shit but I just didn't get behind all of the secrets or lying between these two. I just didn't get why things weren't out in the open or why they hid such small things from some people.<br /><br />Other than that, I really enjoyed this book and getting to meet these characters. This is probably because of how realistic this book was in my eyes and it was also something different for YA books. It could just be me thinking that though.<br /><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_118258265" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/118258265" />
    <a title="~Tina~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2594672-tina"><img alt="~Tina~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411474324p2/2594672.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/118258265?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="~Tina~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="~Tina~" href="/user/show/2594672-tina">~Tina~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=ec-lib">ec-lib</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=read-2010">read-2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer118258265" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8982888095175788006"><b>Some Spoilers</b><br/><br/>Anna has been in love with her best friend Matt since they were young kids and on her 15th birthday all of her wishes came true. Not sure how Matt's sister and Anna's best friend Frankie, will take the news, the relationship becomes a secret and before they could tell her, fate steps in and takes Matt away in a horrible accident. Leaving the the family devastated but also leaving Anna, alone, with only bitter sweet memories and a promised secret.<br/>A year later the family goes on vacat</span>
  <span id="freeText8982888095175788006" style="display:none"><b>Some Spoilers</b><br /><br />Anna has been in love with her best friend Matt since they were young kids and on her 15th birthday all of her wishes came true. Not sure how Matt's sister and Anna's best friend Frankie, will take the news, the relationship becomes a secret and before they could tell her, fate steps in and takes Matt away in a horrible accident. Leaving the the family devastated but also leaving Anna, alone, with only bitter sweet memories and a promised secret.<br />A year later the family goes on vacation, the first one since Matt's death and Frankie comes up with a plan to meet as many guys while there. Only Anna guilt mixed with Matt's memory is weighing her down.<br />How does one move on without erasing the other...?<br /><i> Dear Matt,<br />What is the statute of limitations on feelings guilty for cheating on a ghost?</i><br /><br /><b>Twenty Boy Summer</b> is so not what I expected. It's the kind of story that hits you hard then slowly grabs your hand and walks you through it.<br />It's heart breaking and heart warming at the same time.<br /><br />This was such an amazing book and this is yet another one that I'm kicking myself for not reading sooner ( Alexa, I'm so stalking your shelves for now on babe).<br />At first I wasn't sure that I could sympathize with Anna's lost since Matt was taken away pretty quick in the book, so I couldn't feel a connection to them right away, but as the story went on, Anna took his memories with her and then all I felt was sad. Sad that that the relationship could have been so great, sad that those memories are filled with such sweetness, sad that it had to be over before it ever really begun. But I didn't really walk away from this book feeling sad, there were still a lot of funny and heart warming moments scattered in this book. It's just a fantastic book about loving someone and moving on. How that no matter what happens you get to keep them in your heart always and that's a beautiful thing.<br /><br />So, overall, I loved this book. It was <i>Happy and sad and tragic and whatever</i>, but most of all it was a honest to good read and a wonderful debut!<br /><br />Read it! It's good for the heart:)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8982888095175788006" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1357207557" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1357207557" />
    <a title="☼♄Jülie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20814018-j-lie"><img alt="☼♄Jülie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483253921p2/20814018.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1357207557?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="☼♄Jülie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="☼♄Jülie " href="/user/show/20814018-j-lie">☼♄Jülie </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to ☼♄Jülie  by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/11889829-suzanne">Suzanne</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20814018-j-lie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20814018-j-lie?shelf=women-s-fiction">women-s-fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1357207557" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4603387227905179980"><br/>This is a beautiful story of friendship, that essential ingredient to any meaningful relationship.<br/>Beautifully related by Sarah Ockler, this book has conjured the essence of what it feels like as a teenager to relate to friendships and life experience on a meaningful level. <br/>Her writing takes the reader on an experiential journey of one Summer vacation shared by best friends Frankie and Anna, along with Frankie's parents who are also best friends of Anna's parents.<br/>Each member of this group of four</span>
  <span id="freeText4603387227905179980" style="display:none"><br />This is a beautiful story of friendship, that essential ingredient to any meaningful relationship.<br />Beautifully related by Sarah Ockler, this book has conjured the essence of what it feels like as a teenager to relate to friendships and life experience on a meaningful level. <br />Her writing takes the reader on an experiential journey of one Summer vacation shared by best friends Frankie and Anna, along with Frankie's parents who are also best friends of Anna's parents.<br />Each member of this group of four have "extra baggage" so to speak, and it is this holiday together that will prove challenging for each of them on many levels.<br /><br />I love YA books that transport me back to my youth, especially like this one where lazy summer days at the beach are a feature and young love is all consuming.<br />Some of the best times of our lives can be recalled from that chapter...though not always rosy, when you really think about it those times can also evoke memories of some of the most painful experiences of your life.<br />In fact many of them can be traced back to these origins because this is usually your first experience with facing such trials, they are things which mould us and remind us that emotional pain can be crippling, and is relative to the sufferer.<br /><br />This is a time when you are learning and growing at an alarming rate, experiencing many things for the first time...not always pleasant, often profound, confusing, and memorable. Always edifying.<br />These life experiences are our early teachers in higher education, and as such they are more often than not, hard task masters.<br /><br />I believe this quote by Charles Dickens from A Tale of Two Cities is most befitting of that period in our lives....<br /><br /><i>It was the best of times, it was the worst of times, it was the age of wisdom, it was the age of foolishness, it was the epoch of belief, it was the epoch of incredulity, it was the season of Light, it was the season of Darkness, it was the spring of hope, it was the winter of despair, we had everything before us, we had nothing before us, we were all going direct to heaven, we were all going direct the other way - in short, the period was so far like the present period, that some of its noisiest authorities insisted on its being received, for good or for evil, in the superlative degree of comparison only.</i><br />Charles Dickens, A Tale of Two Cities<br />English novelist (1812 - 1870)   <br /><br />4★s<br />*Many thanks to my GR friend Suzanne for recommending this book, so glad to have read it.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2351701591769301529"><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://inbetweenwritingandreading.blogspot.com/'>http://inbetweenwritingandreading.blo...</a><br/><br/>It shattered my heart to pieces, It gave me the deepest wounds, It made me stronger than ever, And it put me back together. Those are the words I have to say about this book.<br/><br/>At first, when I bought the book, I really didn’t know what I was getting into, I mean, 20 boys? One each day?   <span id="freeText2351701591769301529" style="display:none"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://inbetweenwritingandreading.blogspot.com/">http://inbetweenwritingandreading.blo...</a><br><br>It shattered my heart to pieces, It gave me the deepest wounds, It made me stronger than ever, And it put me back together. Those are the words I have to say about this book.<br><br>At first, when I bought the book, I really didn’t know what I was getting into, I mean, 20 boys? One each day? I thought it would be a simple comedy and a fun read for the summer. How wrong I was.<br><br>Twenty Boy Summer follows Anna through her summer, where she grieves the dead of the brother of her best friend and boyfriend Matt, the only problem, no one knew they were together. So Frankie’s family – and Matts- decide to take a trip to California, where they used to go every summer when Matt was alive, and Anna goes with them, carrying her grieve around, for no one but herself to share; She also carries around her journal, where she talks to Matt and pours everything of her. And then there’s Sam, one of the guys they meet during their 20-boy-summer lookout, Handsome, Intelligent, Understanding, and he grows to love Anna, But Anna is so scared to love him back, for the fear of forgetting Matt. I just found it Heartbreaking, and reminded me a lot of Jandy Nelson’s “The Sky Is Everywhere” in many ways.<br><br>The only thing I didn’t liked much about the novel was Frankie, her best friend, who acted nothing like. Though its easy to understand, but she still seems to selfish, shallow and ignorant to me. But you do get why she is necessary in the story, aside from the fact that she adds a little spark and humor to it.<br><br>Anna was simply a character that leaved a mark on me, and a total opposite to Frankie.<br><br>This is Sarah Ockler’s first novel, and reminded me of Sarah Dessen’s novels, which is a great compliment. Twenty Boy Summer is a story in which I loved to live, and leaved a mark in my heart. Gorgeous, beautifully written, and full of Love. I highly recommend it.<br><br><a href="http://inbetweenwritingandreading.blogspot.com//" rel="nofollow noopener">

<span id="freeTextContainer2248711022955276913">2.5 stars. The beginning and end of the book were great to read and a solid 4 stars. Most of the middle part of the book was 1 star. I'm not sure what else to say. I zipped through the book fairly quickly and liked the idea for the story, but think I wanted more out of the actual vacation and "20 boy challenge" than what was given. There really weren't 20 boys (heck, not even 10!), so the title was extremely misleading. <br/><br/>Mildish spoilers ahead :<br/><br/><b>What I liked :</b><br/><br/>Anna and Matt's relationship. <br/><br/>Anna ste</span>
  <span id="freeText2248711022955276913" style="display:none">2.5 stars. The beginning and end of the book were great to read and a solid 4 stars. Most of the middle part of the book was 1 star. I'm not sure what else to say. I zipped through the book fairly quickly and liked the idea for the story, but think I wanted more out of the actual vacation and "20 boy challenge" than what was given. There really weren't 20 boys (heck, not even 10!), so the title was extremely misleading. <br /><br />Mildish spoilers ahead :<br /><br /><b>What I liked :</b><br /><br />Anna and Matt's relationship. <br /><br />Anna stepping out and finding Sam.<br /><br />Anna learning to work through her lingering feelings for Matt, and finding a way to get some sort of closure.<br /><br /><b>What I didn't like :</b><br /><br />Frankie. The girl was one-dimensional. When we finally got to see her emotions, I didn't care by that point.<br /><br />Every single filler scene. There were a lot. I did some skimming.<br /><br />The loss of virginity felt very anti-climactic (HAH - double meaning).<br /><br />Sam. He was sweet, attractive, attentive, and uh...detached. This relationship sort of confused me. I get it when someone's extremely into another person. I also get casual relationships and flings. For some reason, I felt like the author was trying to sell us that this relationship was a bit of both, and it felt...odd. </span>

<div id="review_1601394630" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1601394630" />
    <a title="NAT.orious reads ☾" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54624224-nat-orious-reads"><img alt="NAT.orious reads ☾" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606165351p2/54624224.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1601394630?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="NAT.orious reads ☾" class="user" itemprop="url" name="NAT.orious reads ☾" href="/user/show/54624224-nat-orious-reads">NAT.orious reads ☾</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316051583" href="/book/show/7306337-twenty-boy-summer">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to NAT.orious reads ☾ by: </span>
      ages 14 -19
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54624224-nat-orious-reads?shelf=standalones">standalones</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1601394630" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18092020883398073212"><u>
  <b>3.75 recovering ★★★✬✩</b>
</u><br/><i>
  <blockquote><b>This book is for you if… </b>you want to learn what it can mean to figure out how to reconcile your most important friendship with a promise you gave to your dead lover. Although flawed, this novel still has tiny perfections that make it a lovely book that should be especially promising to younger readers.</blockquote>
</i><br/><b>⤐ <i>Preface.</i></b><br/><i>20 Boy Summer</i> has been resting on my shelf for the <i>longest</i> time. It was among the first books I put on my to-read-shelf back in 2016 when I opened up this acc</span>
  <span id="freeText18092020883398073212" style="display:none"><u>
  <b>3.75 recovering ★★★✬✩</b>
</u><br /><i>
  <blockquote><b>This book is for you if… </b>you want to learn what it can mean to figure out how to reconcile your most important friendship with a promise you gave to your dead lover. Although flawed, this novel still has tiny perfections that make it a lovely book that should be especially promising to younger readers.</blockquote>
</i><br /><b>⤐ <i>Preface.</i></b><br /><i>20 Boy Summer</i> has been resting on my shelf for the <i>longest</i> time. It was among the first books I put on my to-read-shelf back in 2016 when I opened up this account and I've actually had it at home for like half that time. It took me 3.5 years to finally read it. My tastes have evolved immensely since so I figured this might not be my cup of tea as much as it used to be back then. I turned out to be right.<br /><br /><b>⤐ <i>Overall.</i></b><br />Altogether, this book is well written, thoughtful and deals with a topic that is widely underrepresented in young adult literature. What does grief mean when the person you're grieving is somebody you've known your entire life as your brother, fell in love with at age 10 and finally kissed for the first time just mere weeks ago? How do you overcome the death of your first love after you've only had a few weeks to experience the joys of a new relationship? Were you even in a relationship per se? What is it exactly, that you lost? And how do you handle the fact you kept your love a secret from your best friend and promised your dead lover not to tell her? How do you support your best friend when she lost her brother?<br /><br />I don't wish for anybody to be faced with these questions, especially not at such a young age. Growing up is hard as it is. Emotional at times, this story displays great character growth. The emotional development of the main characters is what drives the plot, which I found very refreshing. <i>Twenty Boy Summer</i> still offers humour and silliness, which lightens up the topic a great deal.<br /><br /><b>I noticed some things that really disagreed with me.</b> They were not reoccurring themes throughout the book and just occurred in one line each. It still thought it important to point them out.<br /><br /><b>⤐</b> <i>fatphobia.</i> Frankie, one of the main characters used to be shy. The first reason a guy comes up with after hearing this is that she must have been fat. (Thanks a lot, mate.) I honestly don't know where to start with that and I also want to spare myself the emotional drainage that would come with an explanation (which would undoubtedly end in a rant). It wasn't taken up again, the character didn't even receive a scolding within the plot.<br /><br /><b>⤐</b> <i>acne.</i> 'He's got backne', even said by teenagers, should not be included in the list of reasons to not date someone, not even as a joke. I know for most this is simply how the world of teenagers (or grown-ups) works, but maybe just a few lines on how this is actually a disgusting and traumatizing mindset to the victims (yes, I am speaking from experience), woven into the plot, would have made all the difference. If you can't manage that, then leave out the topic entirely. Do not make fun of people with acne. Do not use a skin condition, or any kind of condition, against people.<i> Just don't.</i><br /><br /><b>⤐ <i>What’s happening.</i></b><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>‘Anna, when you meet the ocean, you feel it more than you see it. If you’re lucky, that wonderment never fades, and you feel it again every timey ou get back here. You’ll feel it someday.’</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />Never did Anna think she'd see the ocean for the first time without Matt. But now her first love, the person she could only spend a few weeks with in secret, is dead and she never got to tell her best friend, Matt's sister, that they were in love. She promised him not to. But do you keep a promise made to a dead person? And what are the consequences?<br /><blockquote><b>Con:</b><br />⇢ <i>secrets eat you up from the inside</i><br />⇢ <i>grief makes living guilt-free nearly impossible</i><br />⇢ <i>best friend wants to cure virginity with 20 boys within 23 days</i><br /><b>Pro:</b><br />⇢ <i>3 weeks in zansibar at the beach</i><br />⇢ <i>boys are still cute</i><br />⇢ <i>collecting glass shards with ocean as background music</i></blockquote><br />_____________________<br /><b>
  <i> Writing quality + easy of reading</i>
</b> = 4*<br /><br /><b>
  <i>pace</i>
</b> = 4*<br /><br /><b>

</b> = 4*<br /><br /><b>

</b> = 3*<br /><br /><b>

</b> = 5*<br /><br /><b>

<div id="review_194567009" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/194567009" />
    <a title="Stephanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3882912-stephanie"><img alt="Stephanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1296879444p2/3882912.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/194567009?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephanie" href="/user/show/3882912-stephanie">Stephanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3882912-stephanie?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3882912-stephanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3882912-stephanie?shelf=50-book-2011">50-book-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3882912-stephanie?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3882912-stephanie?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3882912-stephanie?shelf=death">death</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer194567009" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13132251494072435729">34 years ago my brother died in a car accident, I was a little over a year old, he was three. I don't remember much about him, save one strange memory of him standing outside the car entertaining me while my mom pumps and pays for gas. I recall the car, the sun sparkling off of the metal on the window and the smell of the summer day mingling with the smell of the gasoline. And, of course, I have the stories, of how he called me Finnie Shell for Stephanie Michelle, how he would chase me around th</span>
  <span id="freeText13132251494072435729" style="display:none">34 years ago my brother died in a car accident, I was a little over a year old, he was three. I don't remember much about him, save one strange memory of him standing outside the car entertaining me while my mom pumps and pays for gas. I recall the car, the sun sparkling off of the metal on the window and the smell of the summer day mingling with the smell of the gasoline. And, of course, I have the stories, of how he called me Finnie Shell for Stephanie Michelle, how he would chase me around the house, how he could make me laugh...it hurts that I only have these stories and not their memories.<br /><br />2 years ago I gave birth to a tiny person, I was a little over 33 years old, she was a surprise. I remember everything about the night I found out I was pregnant, everything about the day the doctor confirmed it, showing us the ultrasound of our little girl already 5 months in the making and every moment anxiously awaiting her arrival. And, of course, I have the stories, of how she calls me Mommy and Mom and sometimes Mommy Stephanie, how she comes to school with me on Saturday Publication work days, how she makes me laugh...it hurts to realize I used to think my life was complete without her.<br /><br />It's these two people, the brother I never knew and the person I didn't know who could make me, well, a better me, that I think about when I think about Twenty Boy Summer by Sarah Ockler.<br /><br />This book has so much in it and it speaks honestly about love, friendship, family and what it means to grieve the loss of a loved one.<br /><br />I am more than willing to believe that when you are still grieving the loss of someone you truly love that having sex for the first time helps to heal the wound, that blocking it out and drinking and pretending to have sexual exploits makes it a little easier to be alive and that when your child dies a piece of you dies and living doesn't even seem possible. I believe that each of the characters in this book acts how people act when their hearts hurt so much they can't feel it.<br /><br />I like that the parents and other grown-ups in this book are ancillary to the true narrative. I do not mind that the girls sneak out of the house to hang out with boys, go to a party by lying and making up imaginary girl friends. I believe that grieving parents who are just as lost as their still alive children, in this case the very lost Frankie, don't know how to act or how to feel, I believe they ignore and believe what they want to believe. Here's what I don't like, here's the part that makes me sad and here's the part that I hope makes me a better parent...neither of the girls talk to their parents about how they feel and I believe Anna's parents, would listen and trying to help. While I don't need to know everything that my daughter is doing or will do I hope that she knows that she can always talk to me and she can always share her most personal thoughts with me. I hope that she knows that I love her no matter what.<br /><br />Everything in this book is real and honest and tender and I wouldn't change a single word of it.<br /><br />My niece is reading this book right now and I know that I'm going to make sure this book finds its way into the hands of my daughter and then we can have a talk about love and friendship and when it's appropriate to have sex and I hope that while I am not her peer she sees me as someone to go to when she needs to do so.<br /><br />While I write this my daughter is singing "Happy Birthday to Mommy", it isn't my birthday until next May, but it sure feels like a celebration.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13132251494072435729" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1047378075" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1047378075" />
    <a title="Aisyah ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13615508-aisyah"><img alt="Aisyah ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1540283017p2/13615508.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1047378075?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aisyah ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aisyah ♡" href="/user/show/13615508-aisyah">Aisyah ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13615508-aisyah?shelf=real-life-drama">real-life-drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13615508-aisyah?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1047378075" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3155339822173650901">This book tells the story of two best friends, Frankie and Anna dealing with the loss of a brother and a lover respectively. They traveled across the country from New York to California for summer vacation a year after his death. In a way, this trip was supposed to be a mark of how 'normal' things are even as Frankie's family struggled to continue life without Matt. <br/><br/><i>“But when he died, I saw -nothing. There was nothing left to see. It happened and it was impossible and beautiful and then it ended</i></span>
  <span id="freeText3155339822173650901" style="display:none">This book tells the story of two best friends, Frankie and Anna dealing with the loss of a brother and a lover respectively. They traveled across the country from New York to California for summer vacation a year after his death. In a way, this trip was supposed to be a mark of how 'normal' things are even as Frankie's family struggled to continue life without Matt. <br><br><i>“But when he died, I saw -nothing. There was nothing left to see. It happened and it was impossible and beautiful and then it ended before it even really began, leaving nothing behind but secrets and broken hearts.”</i><br><br>However, Anna is overwhelmed by the guilt from not telling Frankie that she was in love and had a relationship with Matt, who made her promise to keep it a secret. Anna &amp; Matt planned to tell Frankie after months of sneaking around, unfortunately the secret died with him and Anna was forced to suppress her true feelings from other people. To everyone, she's just his friend, nothing more nothing less.<br><br>This novel is beautifully written. For a beach lover like me, the author's way of writing about the sea, the sand, the atmosphere of being so near to the ocean just struck a chord with me. Plus, the book takes place mainly at Zanzibar Bay, California where Frankie and Anna spend a lot of time swimming, surfing, sunbathing and of course, meeting boys. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1415581698i/11814841._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book was an easy read and it has quite a few light-hearted moments, however it still brings out serious questions like coping with loss of beloved ones, and keeping secrets that could jeopardize your relationship between a person who trusts you. The author also brings forth topics regarding teenage sexuality and what does it mean letting go of someone you deeply loved in order to move on. <br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="3155339822173650901" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_397167854" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/397167854" />
    <a title="Inge" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6278820-inge"><img alt="Inge" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556214992p2/6278820.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/397167854?book_show_action=true">Aug 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Inge" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Inge" href="/user/show/6278820-inge">Inge</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316051583" href="/book/show/7306337-twenty-boy-summer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6278820-inge?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6278820-inge?shelf=all-time-favourites">all-time-favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6278820-inge?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer397167854" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8645945693855674538"><blockquote>
  <i>“When someone you love dies, people ask you how you're doing, but they don't really want to know. They seek affirmation that you're okay, that you appreciate their concern, that life goes on and so can they. Secretly they wonder when the statute of limitations on asking expires (its three months, by the way. Written or unwritten, that's about all the time it takes for people to forget the one thing that you never will.”</i>
</blockquote><br/>When Matt dies, Anna has no idea what to do with herself. Not only has sh</span>
  <span id="freeText8645945693855674538" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“When someone you love dies, people ask you how you're doing, but they don't really want to know. They seek affirmation that you're okay, that you appreciate their concern, that life goes on and so can they. Secretly they wonder when the statute of limitations on asking expires (its three months, by the way. Written or unwritten, that's about all the time it takes for people to forget the one thing that you never will.”</i>
</blockquote><br />When Matt dies, Anna has no idea what to do with herself. Not only has she lost her best-friend-that’s-a-guy, but also the guy that was <i>other</i>. After a month of sneaky meetings (to spare Frankie’s – Matt’s sister – feelings), Anna has no idea what exactly they are. Matt plans to tell Frankie everything on their holiday to California. But they never go. Because Matt dies in a car accident. Exactly one year later, Anna joins Frankie and her parents on a holiday to California. Anna and Frankie vow to meet twenty boys in three weeks, hopefully so that Anna can lose her virginity. It’s a holiday that will change the girls separately and their friendship forever.<br /><br />When I bought <i>Twenty Boy Summer</i>, I was expecting a light, fluffy, chicklit-y read about two girls going on a holiday and the awkward horrors of dating. After quickly scanning a couple reviews, I quickly realised that this was not going to be the case. I’m glad I knew that beforehand, otherwise I might’ve been disappointed. Now I knew what I was getting into. I, however, did not expect it to be as enticing. As it happened, I read this book in one sitting, only to be interrupted by dinner and an episode of <i>That ‘70s Show</i>. It gripped me from page 1 and still hasn’t let me go, even after the final page.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“I just swallow hard.<br />Nod and smile.<br />One foot in front of the other.<br />I'm fine, thanks for not asking.”</i>
</blockquote><br />Because the romance between Anna and Matt isn’t built up but immediately begins with their first kiss, I found it hard to really understand the depth of their relationship and, eventually, Anna’s loss. It is easy to understand Frankie’s grief as a sister and Anna’s grief as a best friend, but not really as a girlfriend-or-not-what-was-she-exactly. Nevertheless, as the book progresses, it’s clearly that even after a year, Anna still hasn’t forgotten Matt in the slightest. Turns out, a holiday in Zanzibar Bay, and particularly a boy named Sam, are exactly what she needed to accept the past and move on.<br /><br />While some parts (mostly Frankie’s parts) are slightly annoying, the story is still a touching and heartfelt one. A story about what it means to love, to be a friend, to be a part of a (broken) family, to grieve. It got to me. It’s as deep as a teenage novel will go. I would definitely recommend this unexpected little gem. I feel richer now.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8645945693855674538" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7769190301238166682">I have been waiting to read this book for ages, and although it wasn't quite as fantastic as I had counted on (maybe my high expectations are to blame?), it was definitely a good read.<br/><br/>I think this book is one of the books that has made me cry the most while reading it. <br/>Having read the plot summary, this was to be expected.<br/>Anna, Frankie and Matt have been neighbours and close friends since childhood. Anna has had a crush on Matt for almost as long as that. On her 15th birthday, all her wishes fin</span>
  <span id="freeText7769190301238166682" style="display:none">I have been waiting to read this book for ages, and although it wasn't quite as fantastic as I had counted on (maybe my high expectations are to blame?), it was definitely a good read.<br /><br />I think this book is one of the books that has made me cry the most while reading it. <br />Having read the plot summary, this was to be expected.<br />Anna, Frankie and Matt have been neighbours and close friends since childhood. Anna has had a crush on Matt for almost as long as that. On her 15th birthday, all her wishes finally come true. They kiss. Most YA novels would probably end here: The heroine gets her dream boy and they live happily ever after … but not in this case. Shortly after their first kiss, Matt dies unexpectedly and leaves Anna alone with their secret and a grief that she can't really express, especially not around his sister and her best friend, Frankie.<br /><b>Twenty Boy Summer</b> takes place one year after the tragic incident. Anna spends her summer with Frankie and her family at their beach house in California. The emotions surrounding Matt's death are still raw, and with memories of earlier, happier summers resurfacing, it is hard to find closure. <br /><br />This situation is the starting point for a sometimes sad, sometimes funny, emotionally intense and beautifully crafted story about love and loss, friendship and family, but first and foremost about moving on and and letting go.<br /><br />While both Anna and Frankie are relatable, realistic and fully fleshed out, I wish I could say the same about the secondary characters. Especially Anna's love interest remains pale concerning the important role he plays and their relationship didn't feel that special to me. Also, while the issues revolving around Frankie's parents are picked up in the beginning, they are never fully explored. I certainly agree that a book doesn't have to bring closure in every possible sense, but this situation seemed fairly important to me. Often times, the scenes when Anna and Frankie are out together with them are partially glossed over and almost always labeled boring. They are something to get over with, where you pretend to have fun, and then run out to meet the boys as soon as possible. I really wished the book would have shown more growth in this relationship.<br />Additionally, the girls' frequent sneaking out and never getting caught began to grind on my nerves towards the end. I have a hard time imagining that parents really are that clueless and uninterested in their daughter’s whereabouts.<br /><br />Nevertheless, <b>Twenty Boy Summer</b> is a book that will stay on my mind not only for the emotional ride it took me on, but also because it clearly is more than the cute and light beach read its cover suggests.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7769190301238166682" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer418148846165518302"><i>Sometimes when I'm with him, something will remind me of Matt. A shooting star, the smell of someone's shampoo, a long laugh, a turn of phrase from someone passing by along the shore. When it happens, I close my eyes, count to ten, and will him to go away. To give me back my memories so that something as simple as a song floating out from behind a bonfire doesn't bring me all the way back to him every time.</i> <br/><br/>It was hard to choose just one quote to start my (gushing) review of Twenty Boy Summer. T</span>
  <span id="freeText418148846165518302" style="display:none"><i>Sometimes when I'm with him, something will remind me of Matt. A shooting star, the smell of someone's shampoo, a long laugh, a turn of phrase from someone passing by along the shore. When it happens, I close my eyes, count to ten, and will him to go away. To give me back my memories so that something as simple as a song floating out from behind a bonfire doesn't bring me all the way back to him every time.</i> <br /><br />It was hard to choose just one quote to start my (gushing) review of Twenty Boy Summer. There were so many - my copy is covered in sticky notes, favourite passages that I wish I had written myself. Seriously, this book is full of beauty, it was so hard not to put a sticky note on every single page.<br /><br />On the cover of my copy, Jo Knowles describes Twenty Boy Summer: "Breaks your heart and puts it back together again." That's exactly how I felt. I admit that in the beginning I didn't feel sympathy for many of the characters but by a quarter of the way through I realised I had fallen in love with them all. Absolutely all of them. Red, Jayne, Frankie, Anna, Sam... Matt. Especially Matt. <br /><br />It's just that kind of book. It sneaks up on you, quietly crawls under your skin, into your heart.<br /><br />There's so much more I could say but I won't - it's better if you go read it and discover how beautiful it is for yourself. <br /><br />Thanks to Nomes for sending one of her copies my way :) </span>

<div id="review_57736136" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/57736136" />
    <a title="Julie Kagawa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2364898-julie-kagawa"><img alt="Julie Kagawa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1257815866p2/2364898.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/57736136?book_show_action=true">May 29, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie Kagawa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie Kagawa" href="/user/show/2364898-julie-kagawa">Julie Kagawa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer57736136&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer57736136" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10358471931673753102">20 BOY SUMMER surprised me. I thought this would be a light read, with lots of boy chasing and gossip and giggling over clothes and makeup and teenage girl things. And while there are certainly elements of that, dig a bit deeper and there is this raw, aching grief festering just below the surface, as everyone Matt loved tries their best to carry on in their own way. I was tempted to roll my eyes at some of the conversations between Anna and Frankie, especially the nonchalant way they were discus</span>
  <span id="freeText10358471931673753102" style="display:none">20 BOY SUMMER surprised me. I thought this would be a light read, with lots of boy chasing and gossip and giggling over clothes and makeup and teenage girl things. And while there are certainly elements of that, dig a bit deeper and there is this raw, aching grief festering just below the surface, as everyone Matt loved tries their best to carry on in their own way. I was tempted to roll my eyes at some of the conversations between Anna and Frankie, especially the nonchalant way they were discussing Anna's virginity, and how this was the perfect time for her to lose it. It was tempting to dislike Frankie, with her shallow, prima donna attitude and her unwillingness to discuss anything but boys, makeup, and sex. But I couldn't, because I knew it was just a fragile cover to deal with the pain of losing Matt. <br /><br />And that's what Sarah Ockler does so well. Matt's ghost hangs over everything, even when he's not being discussed. This isn't a story about boys and summer love and fun on the beach. Its a story about grief, loss, healing, and moving on. I haven't enjoyed a book like this so much in awhile, and I highly recommend it to anyone. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10358471931673753102" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_55819390" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/55819390" />
    <a title="Kami Garcia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250114-kami-garcia"><img alt="Kami Garcia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452664530p2/2250114.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/55819390?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kami Garcia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kami Garcia" href="/user/show/2250114-kami-garcia">Kami Garcia</a>

          added it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer55819390" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1350649716462519692">This is a beautifully written novel about love, friendship, and the things we carry with us long after the moments in which we experience them end. 20 Boy Summer is more than just your average YA romance. It balances an original teenage voice with prose and metaphor that will haunt you long after you put it down. And as a writer, it made me want to re-read every line I've written in the past six months, in an attempt to strive for that sort of perfection.<br/><br/>I fell in love with all the main characte</span>
  <span id="freeText1350649716462519692" style="display:none">This is a beautifully written novel about love, friendship, and the things we carry with us long after the moments in which we experience them end. 20 Boy Summer is more than just your average YA romance. It balances an original teenage voice with prose and metaphor that will haunt you long after you put it down. And as a writer, it made me want to re-read every line I've written in the past six months, in an attempt to strive for that sort of perfection.<br /><br />I fell in love with all the main characters, and had trouble deciding who I loved the most because each of them was so heartbreaking and real. This book will change the way you think about your past, the present, and the places you hold your memories.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1350649716462519692" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
