<div id="review_227304144" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/227304144" />
    <a title="Aly (Fantasy4eva)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1491042-aly-fantasy4eva"><img alt="Aly (Fantasy4eva)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1392555495p2/1491042.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/227304144?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aly (Fantasy4eva)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aly (Fantasy4eva)" href="/user/show/1491042-aly-fantasy4eva">Aly (Fantasy4eva)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1491042-aly-fantasy4eva?shelf=conflicted-thoughts">conflicted-thoughts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1491042-aly-fantasy4eva?shelf=crushing-on-the-cover">crushing-on-the-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1491042-aly-fantasy4eva?shelf=fast-paced-and-engrossing">fast-paced-and-engrossing</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer227304144" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17457782740911502611"><b>Rating: 3.5</b><br/><br/><b>“Don't move, Anna Reiley. Right now, everything is perfect.”</b> <br/><br/>When the boy you love is the brother of your best friend, things tend to get a tad complicated. In Anna's case, the moment Matt kisses her, she knows without a doubt that he's "the one". Anna is overjoyed but Matt wants to wait before he tells his sister, Frankie. The three have always been a trio of sorts, and he fears revealing their relationship too soon could be too much for her.<br/><br/>Give me a break.<br/><br/>I found it really dodgey h</span>
  <span id="freeText17457782740911502611" style="display:none"><b>Rating: 3.5</b><br /><br /><b>“Don't move, Anna Reiley. Right now, everything is perfect.”</b> <br /><br />When the boy you love is the brother of your best friend, things tend to get a tad complicated. In Anna's case, the moment Matt kisses her, she knows without a doubt that he's "the one". Anna is overjoyed but Matt wants to wait before he tells his sister, Frankie. The three have always been a trio of sorts, and he fears revealing their relationship too soon could be too much for her.<br /><br />Give me a break.<br /><br />I found it really dodgey how he kept putting it off. It made me question what his intentions were. However, there's no time to contemplate.<br /><br />Matt is dead, and leaves behind a distraught family and a grieving girlfriend. Whilst her best friend and his sister Frankie has lost herself in partying, Anna spends her days keeping to herself. But it's when the prospect of a holiday arrives that thing really take a turn.<br /><br />Frankie isn't an easy person to like, so I wondered many times why Anna stuck with her. I wouldn't have. Maybe it's the fact that she's a link to Matt, or part of a past she misses that makes her cling on, but even now - I'm conflicted on her. On this holiday, the two sneak out, go boy hunting, and take on anything else rebellious that comes to mind. Whilst originally sworn of boys, Anna soon finds herself caught up with a boy called Sam. He's lovely, of course - if not a little too lovely - bordering on bland.<br /><br />Here is where I started questioning Anna. "What ifs" can eat a person up inside - I get that. What if he had lived, would they have lasted? Did he love her? Was he going to tell Frankie? Soon enough though, personally, I started to feel like she was in love with the idea of being in love with Matt. I think that she spent so long pining over him that she just convinced herself that no matter what, they were going to be together forever. The naive, high school girl mentality. Of course, real life is never that simple. But even after his death, she seems to cling on to this fantasy. But here's the deal. She spends so much of the novel telling us of the sweet moments they shared, of her love for him, only to fall for Sam and realise that what she felt for Matt was nothing compared to how she felt for Sam. *sighs*. Talk about fickle. Don't spend the whole book moaning about how much you love this particular guy, soften me up to the idea and then meet this random guy for a few days, declare yourself in love with him, and then tell me Matt never compared to him. WTF is that? What does that tell me about you?<br /><br />I think her dismissing Matt in that way, *even if it was intentional* bothered me becuse I liked what her and Matt had - no matter how breif. There were some very sweet moments between the two. Their first kiss being a favourite of mine :)<br /><br /><b>“Anna," he said, dragging his frosted fingers through my hair."Don't you know what it means when a boy pulls your hair at your birthday party?" "No." Just, then, I didn't know what anything meant.”</b> <br /><br />I didn't like Frankie, but there were real moments that made me contemplate otherwise at times. I felt there was more depth to her than our protagonist. Sure Anna is hurting, but when I think of the above points regarding Sam, I don't feel so sorry for her anymore. However Frankie has other issues. If you look behind her bitchy attitude, underneath lies a girl who wants to be noticed by her parents. Who wants her parents to catch her sneaking out and tell her she's grounded. She feels lonely and unloved. Sometimes we forget that she's Matt's sister. That maybe this out-of-control Frankie is a mere shell to hide just how much she is falling apart. She was basically betrayed by the two people she loved most. Anna being the protagonist, can tend to make us forget that at times.<br /><br />I liked the book, a lot. It was a fast read, filled with memorable lovely quotes. I just expected to love it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17457782740911502611" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_44948036" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/44948036" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/170420-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1228387079p2/170420.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/44948036?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/170420-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/170420-laura?shelf=old-reads">old-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/170420-laura?shelf=mt-bookpile-2009">mt-bookpile-2009</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer44948036&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer44948036" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4549455932207537734">I wanted so much to like this book and instead was vaguely disappointed by the lack of depth and inner dialogue at several critical points. <br/><br/>This is the story of three friends, Anna, Frankie and Matt (Frankie and Matt are siblings, Anna is the girl-next-door), and how Matt's death changes things. Just before he died, Anna and Matt had started a clandestine relationship while Matt waited for the right moment to tell Frankie. After his death, Anna keeps it all to her self, writing letters/journal e</span>
  <span id="freeText4549455932207537734" style="display:none">I wanted so much to like this book and instead was vaguely disappointed by the lack of depth and inner dialogue at several critical points. <br /><br />This is the story of three friends, Anna, Frankie and Matt (Frankie and Matt are siblings, Anna is the girl-next-door), and how Matt's death changes things. Just before he died, Anna and Matt had started a clandestine relationship while Matt waited for the right moment to tell Frankie. After his death, Anna keeps it all to her self, writing letters/journal entries and "talking" to him, while outwardly portraying her grief as that of best-friend-to-sister-of-Matt. <br /><br />Matt's death wasn't due to carelessness, drunk driving, or anything "teachable": he had a heart defect and was unlucky enough to be driving (with Anna and Frankie) at the time. This was one of those could have happened anywhere/any time events, and so is glossed over. The majority of the book takes place a year later, as his family heads to California for their annual vacation and Anna comes along to help Frankie get over her grief.<br /><br />You see glimpses of what Frankie's going through (dressing more provocatively, smoking, grades going down, acting out) but you never really get a sense of what Anna thinks about this or what she has tried to do other than be there for Frankie. She even goes along with the "20 boy summer" idea without a lot of internal process.<br /><br />Most disturbing was the almost blase way in which Anna's losing her virginity was handled. Dubbed "Anna's Albatross" (and the reason for the 20 boy idea - surely one of them will Do the Deed) by Frankie, you never get how Anna feels about it. When she finally does have sex, any thoughts or emotions are swept away by the drama of Frankie finding out about Matt/Anna. <br /><br />Given that there was a lot of Anna "hearing" Matt's voice, talking to him, thinking about him, I expected something more in the way of self-reflection and internal conflict at times. Anna seemed too passive in places, which didn't ring true. Perhaps as an adult I expected more, and younger (eg, teen) readers will not.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4549455932207537734" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_198801593" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/198801593" />
    <a title="Jodi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5407507-jodi"><img alt="Jodi" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/198801593?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jodi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jodi" href="/user/show/5407507-jodi">Jodi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer198801593" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10015451967247630231"> Ugh. I did not care for this book. I pulled it off the return cart (it certainly circulates often!) and thought it looked like a fun beach read. Ummm, not so much. Right off the bat, in the first chapter, we learn that there is a tragic accident where someone very close to the narrator dies. (I promise, this is not a spoiler - it's on the back cover!)<br/> I was pretty sure at this moment that my hopes of reading a light-hearted beach read were quickly disappearing. What I was left with instead, was</span>
  <span id="freeText10015451967247630231" style="display:none"> Ugh. I did not care for this book. I pulled it off the return cart (it certainly circulates often!) and thought it looked like a fun beach read. Ummm, not so much. Right off the bat, in the first chapter, we learn that there is a tragic accident where someone very close to the narrator dies. (I promise, this is not a spoiler - it's on the back cover!)<br /> I was pretty sure at this moment that my hopes of reading a light-hearted beach read were quickly disappearing. What I was left with instead, was a 16 year-olds quest to lose her virginity. <br />Things that continued to irritate me throughout the book was the author's constant need to point out Frankie's lack of vocabulary. Is this character really that stupid where she mis-pronounces every word?? And if she's that dumb, do we need to keep seeing Anna correct her? The constant corrections were as irritating as the grammatical mistakes.<br /> The other thing that bothered me was the excruciating over-detailing of the story. Ockler felt the need to throw in so many unnecessary details about everything. This, unfortunately, made an un-interesting plot move even slower. However, after spending tens of pages on describing one afternoon at a time, suddenly there was a paragraph that started along the lines of "the next week passed by ..." or whatever and I suddenly felt cheated on the development of the story.<br /> So, I guess that this was a story about death and dealing, bratty best friends and the quest to have sex with a random stranger while on vacation. I don't think that this is one that I will want to recommend to the teens which makes me feel as if I've wasted my evening with reading this book.<br /><br /></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer475322974421500806">This book would be SO much better if it had been through the eyes of the MC's best friend, Frankie. I loved Frankie. She was honest and real and surviving the only way she knew how after her brother's death.<br/><br/>The way that our MC, Anna, described her just pissed me off.   <span id="freeText475322974421500806" style="display:none">This book would be SO much better if it had been through the eyes of the MC's best friend, Frankie. I loved Frankie. She was honest and real and surviving the only way she knew how after her brother's death.<br /><br />The way that our MC, Anna, described her just pissed me off. Every two pages we were reminded that Anna is smarter, that she just <i>doesn't care</i> about her appearance as much, and that she was a Virgin and her friend Was Not. The way that she treated her friend, not outwardly but inwardly, just made me mad.<br /><br />I understand that you looooved Matt but your best friend lost her brother. He died. She lost her brother. Brother &gt; bestfriend/crush anyday. She acted like her hurt was equal to Matt's and Frankie's hurt and it just seemed to rude.<br /><br />I just didn't like a lot about this book and three stars is generous. just because I liked the ending. <br /><br />I expected romance and yeah I got a cute little summer fling but it didn't blow me away. It didn't make me giddy. It didn't make me feel like I was in the book. Frankly, I just didn't feel.<br /><br />I didn't cry when Matt died. I didn't cry when the characters cried. I didn't feel sad when they felt sad. I just didn't feel anything. I'm disappointed with this book.</span>

<div id="review_3374770018" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3374770018" />
    <a title="The Candid Cover (Olivia &amp; Lori)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14451126-the-candid-cover-olivia-lori"><img alt="The Candid Cover (Olivia &amp; Lori)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1549469354p2/14451126.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3374770018?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The Candid Cover (Olivia &amp; Lori)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The Candid Cover (Olivia &amp; Lori)" href="/user/show/14451126-the-candid-cover-olivia-lori">The Candid Cover (Olivia &amp; Lori)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316051583" href="/book/show/7306337-twenty-boy-summer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14451126-the-candid-cover-olivia-lori?shelf=2010-releases">2010-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14451126-the-candid-cover-olivia-lori?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14451126-the-candid-cover-olivia-lori?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3374770018" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16579408060474998566"><a href='https://candidcover.net/twenty-boy-summer-sarah-ockler/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Full Review on The Candid Cover</a><br/><br/>Twenty Boy Summer by Sarah Ockler is a summer read that is able to balance fluff with heavy topics. I enjoyed the leisure atmosphere of the vacation as well as the main character’s dynamic characterization. I also appreciated the nuance with which the author writes about grief. This is an enticing read that is realistic and easy to connect with.<br/><br/>This book follows two best friends on vacation who plan to each have a summer fling by meeting twenty different boys durin</span>
  <span id="freeText16579408060474998566" style="display:none"><a href="https://candidcover.net/twenty-boy-summer-sarah-ockler/" rel="nofollow noopener">Full Review on The Candid Cover</a><br /><br />Twenty Boy Summer by Sarah Ockler is a summer read that is able to balance fluff with heavy topics. I enjoyed the leisure atmosphere of the vacation as well as the main character’s dynamic characterization. I also appreciated the nuance with which the author writes about grief. This is an enticing read that is realistic and easy to connect with.<br /><br />This book follows two best friends on vacation who plan to each have a summer fling by meeting twenty different boys during their trip. Anna goes along with it, but she has a secret: she was dating her best friend’s brother, but he passed away just before they could share the news with Frankie. This tension was interesting to read about, and the way memories of Matt were included add a lot to the story. I wasn’t convinced I would be able to sympathize with this because his death happens so early in the story that he isn’t fully characterized, but the author does a great job showing the effects of his death on Anna and allowing the reader to fully understand the weight of what could have been.<br /><br />❀ GENUINE MAIN CHARACTER<br /><br />I enjoyed Anna’s character. She is genuinely caring and loyal to her friends. Anna is always there for Frankie even though she isn’t okay herself, and I really sympathized with her because of this reluctance to ask for help. She is so strong, but she doesn’t need to be that strong all the time. Ultimately, I liked Anna’s voice, and I thought she was a dynamic character.<br /><br />❀ REALISTIC BOOK<br /><br />One of my favourite parts about this book is the way it is written and the way the author handles grief. The book has its tragic moments, and I liked how the sadness the main character feels is not discounted. Anna still misses Matt, but she is also able to find happiness in her life with another boy while acknowledging the pain she feels. There was a good level of nuance to this book, and this is part of what makes it so realistic.<br /><br />❀ CUTE AND EMOTIONAL<br /><br />Twenty Boy Summer is a contemporary that is both cute and emotional. I enjoyed the suspense of waiting for Frankie to learn the truth, and the main character is complex. I also found the way the author addresses the more serious topics of the book to be well done. I would recommend this to those looking for a more serious summer read that still has moments of fun.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16579408060474998566" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2536978904" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2536978904" />
    <a title="Sam" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/84524539-sam"><img alt="Sam" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532333501p2/84524539.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2536978904?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sam" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sam" href="/user/show/84524539-sam">Sam</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84524539-sam?shelf=stand-alone">stand-alone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84524539-sam?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84524539-sam?shelf=2018-reads">2018-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2536978904" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3244432361383077925">The book was decent, and that's all. It didn't make me laugh, or cry, but it wasn't bad. <br/>Anna goes on a trip with her best friend Frankie to Zanzibar, California. They create their own challenge, Twenty Boy Summer. In which they try to meet twenty boys before the end of the vacation. But Anna doesn't want to meet boys. She still isn't over the death of her first boyfriend, only a little over a year ago. But no one knows that she and Matt dated. And she can't tell anyone one because she made a pr</span>
  <span id="freeText3244432361383077925" style="display:none">The book was decent, and that's all. It didn't make me laugh, or cry, but it wasn't bad. <br />Anna goes on a trip with her best friend Frankie to Zanzibar, California. They create their own challenge, Twenty Boy Summer. In which they try to meet twenty boys before the end of the vacation. But Anna doesn't want to meet boys. She still isn't over the death of her first boyfriend, only a little over a year ago. But no one knows that she and Matt dated. And she can't tell anyone one because she made a promise. And Matt is Frankie's brother. <br />Anna is a blase character. Even though Matt died, and she is grieving. I felt like she didn't have a lot of structure. I wanted to like Frankie, but she made it hard with all her trashy friend moves. Frankie's parents were horrible. Their son died, but they still have a daughter, and they should get a clue. <br />Sam was a weak love interest. It was almost aggravating how understanding he was. He never got mad at Anna. And he didn't really have a reason to, but he was all most too perfect. <br />It was an easy read, but I did put off really reading it for awhile, before I hunkered down and read the whole thing.<br />When Frankie found out about Matt and Anna's relationship, and had her whole episode. I wanted to fight. I mean come on girl, he was your brother, but you weren't the only person who lost him. <br /><br />3/5 stars, utterly average.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3244432361383077925" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Farren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29738019-farren"><img alt="Farren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438296630p2/29738019.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1658950568?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Farren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Farren" href="/user/show/29738019-farren">Farren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316051583" href="/book/show/7306337-twenty-boy-summer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29738019-farren?shelf=ammp-fairytale">ammp-fairytale</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29738019-farren?shelf=ya-contemporary-romance">ya-contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29738019-farren?shelf=own-paperback">own-paperback</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1658950568" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer661458450835801349"><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>It took me a few chapters to get used to Sarah's writing, but I loved it by the end of the book. I wasn't sure it was the book for me, especially because I found Frankie to be so unlikable, but it gets better as you read on. I have never lost anyone I was close to, so I can't speak from personal experience, but I think I'd still recommend this book to someone who has. It shows how grief can change people in completely different ways and how/when/if it's okay to move on.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Riddhi." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51923652-riddhi"><img alt="Riddhi." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593254363p2/51923652.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Riddhi." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Riddhi." href="/user/show/51923652-riddhi">Riddhi.</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2010534736" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16627738549563326931"><s>5 stars</s><br/>"All the stars and bundles of care packages."<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1534650296i/26153724.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>A lot of authors have perfected the art of heartbreaking. And guess who just got added to the list: Sarah Ockler. <br/><b>
  <u>When I started the book</u>
</b><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1534650296ra/26153726.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>
  <u>When I was halfway through the book</u>
</b><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1534650296ra/26153727.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>
  <u>When I finished the book</u>
</b><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1534650296ra/26153723.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I can't bring myself to write a review for this book. This was so heartbreaking and gloomy. The more I read the more I couldn't tear myself away from it.<br/><br/><u>
  <b>
    <i>What happens when death visits home?</i>
  </b>
</u><br/>Sarah Ockler has painted a vivid and bl</span>
  <span id="freeText16627738549563326931" style="display:none"><s>5 stars</s><br>"All the stars and bundles of care packages."<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1534650296i/26153724.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>A lot of authors have perfected the art of heartbreaking. And guess who just got added to the list: Sarah Ockler. <br><b>
  <u>When I started the book</u>
</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1534650296ra/26153726.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>When I was halfway through the book</u>
</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1534650296ra/26153727.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>When I finished the book</u>
</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1534650296ra/26153723.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I can't bring myself to write a review for this book. This was so heartbreaking and gloomy. The more I read the more I couldn't tear myself away from it.<br><br><u>
  <b>
    <i>What happens when death visits home?</i>
  </b>
</u><br>Sarah Ockler has painted a vivid and bleak image of the answer in her book.<br><br><u>
  <b>
    <i>What if someone you were close to dies, and you can't even mourn?</i>
  </b>
</u><br>Anna is going through a similar situation and it's sad to watch her bury her feelings to put up a friendly face.<br><br><b>“If you could, would you ask for moonbeams in a heart of glass? <br>For sun rays on the silver sea? <br>Or would you ask for me?”</b><br><br>Anna Riley from New York is my favorite.<br>I can totally relate to her. Sarah Ockler's writing is similar to Kelley York's minus the dark aspects. Her writing gives us a vivid insight into the characters' heads.<br>And that's what happened here. <br><br><b>"I make a mental note to ditch the makeup tomorrow. Then I get mad at myself for letting some boy that I just met dictate what I do<br>with my own face. Then I get mad at myself for getting mad at myself and remember that I, too, prefer the natural look.</b><br><i>
  <b>See? This is exactly why I don’t want to get involved with anyone."</b>
</i>.<br><br>I kinda hate Frankie. That girl is a drama queen.<br>I know she suffered huge loss but she was kinda mean to Anna and that cannot be justified.<br>Princess Perino can't be forgiven. Still, I made peace with it by the end of the book.<br><br><b>Warning</b>:- This is not a love story. This story is more about letting go when needed.<br><br>I am actually quite impressed with the blurb of the book. It doesn't give away the huge twist that takes place at chapter 4. So, people go with the idea that it is a summer love story.<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[A particular scene with a comparison to a sea mermaid is my favorite part of the book. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1534650296ra/26153725.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>While reading, if you're done till chapter 5 or 6, please listen to "Comes and Goes" by Greg Laswell.<br>Totally goes with the scenario.<br><br><b>
  <u>Conclusion:- Please read it. </u>
</b><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('yYTzki64EUxtQyqVeDhaROfH3ZfwWuHcqfhsqzaQ7VUsiS3Y9VK6QvBKEbZp5qMPMT3pHH4gUsHe2pv2AkConA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nu9a3usMMeFZWK1NHZm2ZzbwTvsfQZOXFV+h0VgVAmx74oSUMOaa78RRlm4MR08s4Ap6cJE7IIpifVaMbMVHpQ==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3130678773228990098">Sarah Ockler is the bestselling author of six young adult novels: The Summer of Chasing Mermaids, #scandal, The Book of Broken Hearts, Bittersweet, Fixing Delilah, and Twenty Boy Summer. Her books have been translated into several languages and have received numerous accolades, including ALA's Best Fiction for Young Adults, Girls' Life Top 100 Must Reads, Indie Next List, and nominations for YALSA</span>
  <span id="freeText3130678773228990098" style="display:none">Sarah Ockler is the bestselling author of six young adult novels: The Summer of Chasing Mermaids, #scandal, The Book of Broken Hearts, Bittersweet, Fixing Delilah, and Twenty Boy Summer. Her books have been translated into several languages and have received numerous accolades, including ALA's Best Fiction for Young Adults, Girls' Life Top 100 Must Reads, Indie Next List, and nominations for YALSA Teens' Top Ten and NPR's Top 100 Teen Books. <br /><br />Sarah is a champion cupcake eater, tea drinker, night person, and bookworm. When she's not writing or reading at home in New York City, she enjoys taking pictures, hugging trees, and road-tripping through the country with her husband, Alex.<br /><br />Visit her website at sarahockler.com or find her on Twitter or Facebook.</span>
